RATING: 6.4
This is a true co-op in every sense of the word. Incredibly fun with new people and people new to gaming as player interaction level is high but ap potential is low. It's actually pretty tricky to win solo and the decision making process is just about right for light distraction. - Recommended by John L., GeekSyndicate and just about everyone else.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a great family themed game. It's made even better by the Wizard's Tower expansion. We like the Co-Op feel, where you have to work as a team to "win", yet it's nice adding up your monster kills at the end to see who was the better warrior. This is a great "thematic victory", as you can all relish in the victory, but still have a way to strive to be the best.

It's also nice how it plays out that if you are too focused on "winning" for yourself, you'll doom the team.

Great family game. A keeper.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
A coop game that has enough flexibility in the rules to let you play the way you want and still provide for a fun game. The completely cooperative game is a great family game. The rules are simple enough that younger kids can get in on the fun. The game does require some thoughtful planning ahead and that would be the limiting factor on the age level needed to play although I'm sure a young child in a family would still have a blast helping mom and dad kill the monsters to protect the castle. The coop with a winner version provides enough opportunities for backstabbing your fellow players to still make it fun. But it's a tough line to walk since not helping your fellow players here and there can end up pushing the momentum over to the monsters really easily. The game can have some wild swings in momentum. A couple of tile draws can really swing the balance in a big way so watch out and keep an eye on what nasty tiles are already out of the bag. The Overlord version of the rules takes the game in a new direction and adds full competitive play in a similar fashion to Scotland Yard or even Ghost Chase with one player against the rest. The game works just fine with a good range of players (1-6) but the planning aspect and card trading really come out in games with more players.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
I had shied away from rating this game because I had only played it a couple of times. This has truly been a year of co-ops for me so I was worried that this one would not stand out. That's not true at all. Although Pandemic is likely just as fast as this game and the decisions might be meatier, I would say that this is just as fun because of the fact that it is only semi-cooperative. I've played it about half cooperative half standard and I have to say I prefer the standard rules quite a bit.

It makes the game tense, but you have to have the right group to get into it. I'm interested to try some of the different variants in the game such as the overlord or the my castle is my home variant, or the variant where players do not start with any walls. Truthfully I can see this game being played a lot. Here's to hoping some expansion sets come out with different monsters or effects!

RATING: 6
Loved the short quick and chaotic feeling this game brought the first few times I played it at a small convention. 

Later my roommate bought the game and we played it on and off for a few years. It seems to run between utter chaos and walk in the park but when you got the tension and chaos right the old spark was there.

Pro: Fast Pass, co-op chaos experience, players work together to stop a never ending onslaught of orcs, light hearted fun that is easy to teach and fast to set up and play with some good moments at the table.

Con: Can get repetitive, I think we over played it. Maybe more of a filler or intro game, I don't miss it since our copy moved to BC. 

We played it on and off for a few months, still super fun and easy to teach. But started to feel repetitive after a while. Still a great game, I don't think I would turn down a game per say but I am more likely to pick up the newer Dead Panic! for the new theme and card variation.

RATING: 4
A coop that just doesn't hit the mark. The base game is too deterministic as the choices are usually pretty obvious. The expansions definitely improve the overall gameplay giving the players more to work with and making the monsters more interesting...but it also adds significantly to the length to a game that was already overstaying it's welcome. Even with more stuff, the game starts to feel "samey" as the monsters really aren't all that different from each other. Also, the expansion content adds fiddliness and rules overhead and if you don't have someone who is very familiar with the extra rules and abilities, expect to refer to the rulebook often. If I'm looking to play a light/medium coop with a few friends, Pandemic easily is the better option.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This is a very nice, streamlined cooperative game.  The rules are really straightforward, and it plays in a very quick timeframe.  Some of the decisions seem a bit more rudimentary, but that makes for a nice change for people who don't like so many options on their turn (which can slow down some players in a game like Pandemic.)  I think these aspects of the game make it an ideal cooperative game for young people.  If you play fully cooperative you can really teach them the mechanisms as you play and, even if it takes them awhile to understand how things work, they will still feel like they are contributing on their turn by slaying monsters and building walls.

As for playing with adults, I can see this one also working in that scenario as well, thanks to the Master Slayer rules.  Adding in that competitive element will challenge players to balance their own selfish desires with the needs of the overall team.  Personally I lean more towards the fully cooperative game, but I like having the competitive option.  This game has a fun theme that is very well executed (I especially love when a boulder goes rolling through crushing monsters as it makes its way to the castle.)  Sure the decisions are fairly straightforward and the game is a little lacking in strategic depth, but for a silly fun competitive/cooperative experience, I don't think you will go wrong with this game.

(KIDS) Seems quite clever... more so than I was expecting.  When we played it with the whole family, we didn't hurt the monsters when they took out a wall or tower and we were demolished.  My wife and I tried it and followed the rules properly.  We obliterated the game and it wasn't even close.  Hopefully, we can find some middle ground.

I'm finding that I'm just not enjoying this game.  It seems like it should be neat with a fun theme and some clever mechanics that keep the game simple and should create some tough situations.  Maybe I need to play the game with 10 year old boys, because with adults and younger kids it just is not working.  It never feels like everything stacks up quite right... maybe it's too random.

I've played it five times and not sure when (or if) I'll play it again.  Maybe when my son is older, I'll try it with him again.  Maybe not.  Seems like there are so many better options for cooperative kids' games (e.g. Forbidden Island).

In my two most recent plays with my 3 and 6 year old kids, the games were very close and quite a bit more fun.  The kids are really loving this game so I've bumped up the rating a full point.

RATING: 4

RATING: 6.5
I've always played this cooperatively, ignoring the "winner" calculation of who scores the most kills. This is a game my son wanted to pick up after watching it played on Tabletop, and he can still be talked into playing it on occasion.

Waves of enemies pour in toward your castle, and you try to fight them off. A little weird in that you often hope for a well-placed boulder attack: sure, it might take down one of your towers, but if it did enough damage to the enemy on the way in then it's worth it. Becomes more complicated and difficult if you add in the Wizard's Tower expansion.

RATING: 7
This is a great tower defense game that is very simple to learn and pickup and can be played in a reasonable amount of time. This game is a coop which is a big plus in my book. It's also fairly hard to win at times which is nice to provide a challenge in that way. The generic fantasy theme fits well for what this game is, a light castle defense romp. The game can be played solo which is always a plus as this provides a way to learn the game and practice strategy while alone. There are a couple of great expansions out that add some depth. Overall this is a great pickup and one that I think a family can enjoy for multiple plays. I recommend getting this one.

RATING: 6.5
This game is a hybrid between a cooperative game and a competitive game.  Cooperative in that, if the players don't work together, everyone loses.  However, once it's obvious that the game can be won; it's competitive.  Yet, by then it's too late, if you weren't getting your kills; you're in trouble.  There's a tug between trading to help the group and holding a useful card to help yourself. I like the game, but I don't take it seriously.  Card draws and timing have just as much to do with the final winner as individual play does.  More a game of tactics than strategy.

It's pleasant enough, but not compelling, and I'm not sure we need to play this again.

RATING: 7
I enjoyed Castle Panic, but it's a tough sell. It manages tension quite well, and is fairly short, and so has a good fun factor. On the scale of coops, it's pretty simplistic, simpler even than Forbidden Island, and Forbidden Island is about as low as I think I'd want to go (although obviously Space Alert demonstrates that complexity isn't the answer either). The opportunity for meaningful player cooperation is fairly limited, just one card swap each turn, and the tactics are pretty straightforward and less intuitive than they should be. It's honestly a pretty fun game because it manages the drama pretty well, but as a game it's caught in the crossfire between Pandemic and Cutthroat Caverns, both of which are vastly more interesting and replayable in my opinion. Not bad, and I enjoyed playing, but not one I feel a need to add to my collection or one I would ever suggest playing myself.

Sleeved
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Awesome game. Just played my first set of games yesterday. Rules are quite simple but the tension it creates with the never ceasing march of monsters towards your castle is absolutely riveting!
 
I lost my first two games badly, but on the third try I vanquished my foes with just two out of six towers standing. It was that close! I would like to think it was due to my impeccable game playing but if the truth is to be told I was lucky in drawing the right cards at the right time. Nevertheless you never know what's going to happen each turn.
 
Best thing I like about this game as opposed to playing with 1 to 5 other players is the down time for solitaire play is incredibly short - 30 seconds between each turn. And in those 30 seconds you are still actively involved in rolling the die for the monsters and moving them towards the castle.
 
Out of the hundreds of games in my collection I would say this is the [b]BEST[/b] solitaire game in the light weight category. (By light weight, I mean the complexity weight rating is between 1.0 and 1.6). Most games in that category offer fewer strategic options and lack the thematic atmosphere that this game so successfully provides! Beautiful board, menacing chits, quick setup, and standup walls and towers, makes this a winner!

The balance of the game seems to be just right and the different variants (full co-op, semi co-op or 1 vs many) all change the game enough to change the experience, while the rules stay simple.

I would recommend this game to everyone except perhaps the most die-hard gamers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
My 3yo son cannot get enough of Castle Panic. We play with all the cards up, but normal rules after that. 

I am completely stunned and amazed at how this game has taken a hold on him. Every new monster that comes out is studied with questions like, "Daddy, why is he wearing an eye patch? Did the archer get him in the eye?!!"

When the Special Monsters come out we open the rule book to look at the big pictures of them, which usually turns into an impromptu story based around their appearance and their special ability. At night, the only bed time stories I tell are based on the Castle Panic monsters. In fact, we now have the adventures of Miyu (me-you) the Goblin, which is an ongoing saga from night to night - the story started (months ago) when Miyu was forced to flee back into the enchanted forest from the courageous Hero who was protecting the castle. (In the latest episode he and his loyal side kick - Spotty the Flighter Spider - battle the wicked witch to get her broom, because it was made out of a branch from the enchanted talking tree, which had been cursed and could no longer talk - the only thing that could lift the curse was the return of the branch (the witches broom)).

Recently I saw the Castle Panic rules laying on the floor up in his playroom. He had taken them out of the box and was flipping through them like it was one of his books and he was telling his little 2yo brother all about the wild and wonderful Castle Panic world!

This game is worth every single penny. We essentially use it as a prop to tell big elaborate stories over the evening.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
This is a great game for nearly any group, especially family or casual-gamer friends. My mom even enjoys playing Castle Panic!

To whom it may concern, this game is VERY random, with player abilities largely based on card draw. Monsters are (literally) drawn out of a black bag and placed randomly. This can make the game very swingy and chaotic, which I think is perfect for what it is. Some turns, everything seems to be under control, and then you'll suddenly draw the Draw 4 More Monsters token and a Troll King, and everyone around the table panics again!

The game can be played solo, which some people enjoy quite a bit. However, what I really love about Castle Panic is laughing and slaying monsters with some friends or family, cheering yourselves on when you're doing really well and groaning when that Giant Boulder doesn't mow down all the monsters for you. Trading with the other players around the table can also make a huge difference in your ability to deal with monsters, and if you're dealing with some pretty cutthroat players, it can quickly become a negotiation game. I've given Castle Panic a try solo, and it just didn't seem to have the same life and frenetic energy.

But still! This is a fun, light game good for almost any group. The rules are incredibly simple and intuitive, and everyone I've played with seems to jump in and have a blast every time.

RATING: 7
This is a simple game in the impending disaster genre, but the components and rules are designed very nicely.  This is high quality and it shows.  Although I like the game, I don't love it - perhaps it's too simple?  But have only played it with 2 - would be curious to try it with more players.

UPDATE: Although this is harder with additional players due to card distribution and limits on trading, it's also more exciting.  So the multi-player challenge lives up to the games promise.  I'm upgrading the rating for this a bit.

Downside - you can win and lose on the die roll.  Roll the same number too often and you're just screwed.

RATING: 8
SOLO PLAY:

1 Player Minimum
6 Player Maximum
I really enjoy this game. I find it too easy but with some variations it makes it fun and exciting again. I look forward to playing it. I find that I like this game much better playing solo. It is more difficult with 1 player and it goes real fast. I'm increasing rating since solo play is so much fun.

SET UP NOTES:
-Set up Towers and walls. Randomly place the Wizards Tower in place of a normal Tower.
-Shuffle Castle Cards and Wizard Cards.
-Remove appropriate tokens to play with expansions.
-Draw 6 tokens (before adding Harbringer Tokens) for each Archer space before the game, excluding bosses and effect tokens. Roll d6 to determine which arc they start in.
-Add 3 random, unseen Harbringer Tokens to the Monster Bag.
-If SOLO play, draw 6 cards.
-Begin Game!

RULES NOTES:
-Only way to get Wizard Cards is during step 2. Discard and Draw 1 card. The draw may be from the Wizard Card deck.
-NECROMANCER: Monsters....not effect tokens.

-SOLO PLAY NOTES:
-If you discard two cards during step 2: Discard and Draw, you may draw 2 Wizard Cards.

RATING: 8
GREAT cooperative gateway game!
I use this one to introduce people to co-op games, because I've found Pandemic to be a bit overwhelming to people due to the high number of options mixed with strategy. Castle Panic still has options and strategy, but not so much to be confusing. The color matching aspect makes it easy to learn, and the board is layed out easily in the different ranges of attacks. Every new turn that brings more monsters ratchets up the tension, but it also brings more opportunities for strategic play. Being able to trade cards with other players helps, as does the player count going up to 6 people. I've played this with a 47 year old and a 9 year old at the same table, and we all enjoyed it!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
A light, fun game that plays very well solitaire.  There are more important decisions in this game than it seems like at first glance - and the best solutions are not always the obvious ones.  There is more than just a little luck involved, but you *do* have to prepare for what is potentially going to happen if you want to win.  It is almost *always* a tense game right down to the last turn.

The 1st expansion is truly awesome and changes my rating on this game from a 7 to a 8.  Would never even consider playing without it now.

Gets bonus points simply because it is so good, fun, and quick to play solitaire.

RATING: 8.5
Terrific co-op game for children, young adults, and non-gamers. It's easy to learn and it teaches a variety of gaming concepts including planning ahead, teamwork, and even some simple probability. My 4 year old daughter loves the game. The violent theme may be a bit too much for small children, but it's easy enough to say that the archers and knights are "chasing away" the mean monsters rather than killing them.  

As a gamer's game, I'd rate this somewhat lower- probably 6.5 or 7- but it is still very enjoyable, with an interesting theme and fun artwork.  

One of the biggest draws here is the ability to customize the game in so many ways. For younger players, there are rules to simplify by removing some of the harder monster tokens. There are also rules for solitaire play, and a version where one player controls the monsters!  I expect my family will continue to have fun with this one for a long time, and as my girls grow older, we can incorporate more of the "regular" rules. Overall, I'm very pleased with the purchase.

RATING: 5
This is more of a sit back and chill game with friends.  I don't like that the person who gets the highest point count in kills wins the game, as it seems to defeat the purpose of a shared cooperative win.  I've played with a few folks who take getting the most kills seriously and it makes the game not fun.

Also the game gets pretty repetitive after the fourth or fifth play when you realize that there's a way to win the game every time, but that's when you ramp up the difficulty with one of the many options listed in the rule book.

Despite all that, the game can be fun. I think this game probably works best as a family game or a younger kids game.  If I owned this when I was a youngster I would have been all over it, and when I turned old and grey (wait, that's starting to happen!) I'd look back and fawn nostalgically over it and weep for my lost childhood.

The expansion also makes this game a good bit better.

RATING: 5
Castle Panic is a cooperative game of tower defense. Cooperative games need to be challenging in order to entertain but Castle Panic fails on that front: the game is neither particularly difficult to win, nor are the player actions required to get there particularly hard to come up with. In fact, moves are mostly obvious and semi-automatic. As such, Castle Panic doesn't work all that well for gamers. I can see it become hoot with younger children, however.

RATING: 6
A fun time generally and a game that really promotes the co-operative spirit. The way the card trades is set up also helps build on the co-op. This game is very light, with the cards in hand pretty much deciding how things are going to go, with a number of other random elements as well. That being said, the game manages to sustain tension by the way the monsters attack the castle. As well, the way in which players must plan is effective and doesn't cause much brain-burning. The game doesn't last too long either, but can't imagine I'd want to play this more than a few times. Must get stale. However, I would definitely see this as a great entry game for kids who will eventually get into heavier games. For that it has my respect. We all won! Only one tower remained with the monster right on its base. Phew! Played regular rules where a player got to be named the 'Super Slayer'. Points system not really necessary, though, and could mess up the win if someone gets greedy!

RATING: 6
I believe my wife got this for me as a birthday gift a few years ago. By no means a bad game, but after a few games I find it somewhat dull - the special abilities in the deck are the most interesting part of the game to me, but there seems to be too few of them. I think I would like this game far more (and it would have far more replayability overall) if there was a secondary way of obtaining/purchasing extra ability cards, rather than just hoping you draw them on a turn where they could be useful.

I recall reading that the expansion helps to keep this game a bit more interesting, so I may look into picking it up at some point, but for the time being, I think there are many, many other games that I'd rather play instead.

RATING: 7
Bought this for just over 20 bucks at Barnes and Noble on sale, and it's been my best purchase for family game nights in quite some time.  Most games either seem to bore my wife, are too complex, or the theme is just too much for her.  This game was near perfect for her AND my daughter, and still appealed to the fantasy geek in me.

Our first playthrough, 3 players (wife, daughter, myself) was a loss at the last minute.  The last monster on the board took out the last tower on my daughter's turn.  After many discards, trades, etc. it came down to the wire, and we just had unlucky card draws (Being that the bugger was in the castle really hurt...lol).

Wife loved it, my daughter was disappointed at first that we lost, but then was glad that we came so close and immediately asked to play it again.  This game has been just the right fit for our "Family game nights", appealing to everyone (Which is REALLY hard to accomplish in this house...lol).

Second playthrough, we won with 1 wall and all but one tower remaining (a boulder took it down, but also wiped out the Goblin King, a Goblin, and an Orc on it's way in!).  The game was still very tense at times, especially when we first started, and it seemed like everything was just flooding the board from all areas.

My soon to be 7 year old daughter, was starting to grasp more of the "Strategy" of holding onto certain cards, and looking more into who to trade with, so repeated plays of this will only help her to grow in relation to strategy/planning in games.  She also won the "Master Slayer" title at the end, besting me by 2 points.

RATING: 8
What an awesome game.  The game is fun and tense at the same time. The game has a few variations, which allow you to play it to your liking, which is a very nice bonus. Their is even a solo version that is a lot of fun. I have yet to beat it solo, but continue to have fun trying.

The components are very nice and I love the monster chits and how you rotate them for their hit points. Absolutely clever, This is a great game for everyone including family, children and gamers. The game plays quick and most people will want to go at it again. Depending on the number of players the game can be tough. Especially the solo version, but it just keeps you coming back for more. If you find the game too easy. Well there are varients to increase the difficulty level for that also.

I highly recommend this game to everyone. You'll surely get your moneys worth from this game. Especially beings that it is pretty cheap to begin with.

Many thanks to boardgameswithscott.com and Tom Vasel for their excellent and informative reviews on this game.

RATING: 7.5
Castle Panic is a simple, fun cooperative game. It's easy enough to play with family or non-gamers, but engaging enough to play with gamers.

The basic game may feel a little deterministic, with there being pretty clear correct actions, but it is very fun nonetheless.

I'd recommend, however, that if you're playing the game with a gaming group, you should consider getting the Wizard's Tower expansion. It brings the game to a higher level of complexity and difficulty. It will force you to really take some time to strategize.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.5
Fun, but flawed. 
After you play a few times you realize that there is almost always one exclusive "right" action to take on any given turn. So, you perform that right next action, then the game takes a turn and beats everyone to a pulp.
Repeat.
This is a "boss" game players dream, because they can tell everyone what to do, ignoring any attempt at individual free-thinking, and then ignore suggestions from the group when it's their turn.
And that's the big flaw. There's no wiggle room for free- thinking. it's an on-the-rails roller coaster, but unlike a roller coaster, it's a little too long.
The game does provide tense fun for a cooperative group, who are willing to talk out the best move and not take advantage of more timid players.

RATING: 7
We hadn't played this until recently because we had always assumed that this was more a kids game due to the game board building. We had some free time, I couldn't walk anymore, so we slid into the demo booth at BGG.Con 2016 to play the newest expansion.

We were very wrong and I am more than a tiny bit ashamed of how long we have missed out on this very fun and almost completely cooperative game. Our demo involved one very long chain of evil happening to our board and we laughed all the way through it.

The mechanics are simple and it only took a full round to grasp it all. It's the simplicity that ensures that the gameplay remains fun and action-packed. 

We loved this game so much we picked it and the latest expansion up and then walked over to the handmade bag vendor, I think Blue Fairy?, and bought a luxurious and bright red microsuede bag with a colourful goblin warrior embroidered on it to hold all the monster game pieces.

Basically, we enjoyed this game so much that minutes after we bought it we had already customized the game experience for ourselves.

RATING: 7
A co-operative game in which the players are trying to defend a castle from hordes of attacking orcs etc. There's a competitive dimension too it as well, as players compete to kill the most monsters.

I played it once with 5 other hardened gamers and we found the competitive side really hampered our ability to deal with the monsters... so we lost. 

I think it might work better as a pure co-op game.. and may be more suitable for a family setting, than for strategy gamers (unlike, say, Pandemic).

RATING: 7
Yet another cooperative game provided by a friend.  We enjoyed the theme of the game and the rather simple ruleset.  There's nothing entirely too deep here, but one person can monopolize the strategy to winning if you aren't careful.  That's an inherent problem with cooperative games and it rings through during Castle Panic.  If you don't see a move right away, your friends will be sure to let you know what you should do for the benefit of the group.  This may detract from new players as they just feel like a pawn from another player instead of feeling like they're involved and belong.  

I'm way too guilty of thinking for others myself, always trying to see the win condition in my head.  All in all though, a fun game to spend some time with friends.  Doesn't require your utmost attention, but still feels satisfying when you win.

RATING: 2
I'm not sure I'd play this again with three. The game is simply drawing cards and then playing them to kill monsters that are rushing upon your castle, from all six sides! This feels like that scene in Aliens where the marines are being attacked, and slaughtered, from all directions. The board even reminds me of the scanner in the movie. From that perspective, it is an intense, if not hilarious semi-cooperative game.

From a mechanics perspective, this is simply idiotic. It's dumb like War is dumb. Draw some cards, play some cards, kill some monsters. Where is the strategy? You can trade one, and only one card with another player--I suppose that counts as strategy. Leave me out of this one, as this smells like another 'zombie' game like Last Night on Earth, which I detest, or that other horseracing game that is all luck--I won't mention it by name.

Update (1/26/11): Who am I kidding? Never going to play this again. It's a '2'.

It's very easy to learn, little down time, and it is a co-operative game with a non-offensive theme - great for families (and not bad as a solitaire game either).

2013-11-26

Initial Rating: 5.0 (November 2013)

Lately, I have been drifting away from this kind of Co-Op game. It is a simple game with lots of uncontrollable luck (a huge minus in my book), easy decisions and alpha player problems. It is fun to play from time to time, some people have a blast playing this but it is way too simple for my taste. IMO all the decisions are kind of obvious, so you win or lose due to the luck of the draw. 

The game has great components and art. The monster bag is very nice to look at. The game is way better than Pandemic and  miles ahead from Flash Point. I like the theme (love fantastic settings)  and the game mechanics are very easy to grasp and teach. This is a family game, perfect to introduce new gamers to the hobby. 

I won‚Äôt be requesting this anytime soon, I won‚Äôt say no if I‚Äôm invited to a game of this, but if I won‚Äôt feel sad if I don‚Äôt play Castle Panic ever again. Not enough game for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Castle Panic is a special case game.  When I saw the reviews, I saw so much potential for co-op fun.  However, the first game I ever played gave me a couple of feelings.  One, it is harder than it looks (my wife and I actually lost).  Second, there seems to be more dictating than co-op work.

I caught the dictating right away and prevented myself from trying to coach the game as much as possible to let my wife enjoy the thinking process for herself.  The game is simple enough and we end up winning the second game.  Then the game became overly simple immediately after that win.  The amount of cards, types of enemy, special effect monster tokens etc. all became too predictable.

I then tried a solo game, it got harder again, however there is just no fun in a solo game.  I rather fire up the computer and play something else with less work.

We finally got to try this in a 4 player setup, and through my group's eyes, I can see their expression and the fun I found in the game the first time I played.  This was played as a filler between two bigger games.  We decided to go for it again and play a second game just to see how well we do after they learned the rules.  This time we played the hardcore mode with no walls to start.  We donkey stomped that game and pwnt the horde...

I found that in that second game, the dictating came back but I've always tried to control myself and everything turned out fine.  The dictating isn't so much one person forcing the other to do stuff, but it was that suggestions kept rolling in from all sides forcing the active player to feel uncomfortable about "breaking up the group" sorta speak.  That hurts this game a LOT!  The fear of not being a team player is making this game less enjoyable than I first thought.

My rating of a 6 means that it is a game that's better than ok...  There are good sides to it, but it isn't a game I would pull off the shelf to play because I craved it.

Now with all said and done, I'm still keeping my copy.  I see the huge potential to teach kids and gateway them to bigger better board games with this game.  I think if scored with kids in mind, I would totally give this game an 8.  This simple game to adults can be immense fun and challenging to a group of 5 - 10 year olds I presume.  I'm going to have a daughter soon, and my nephew will be 5 in 3 1/2 years. (2011)  This game will see a TON of playing time when they come of age...

RATING: 8
This is a quality game, with the caveat that it can get kind of boring without any expansion content (which we have not yet purchased). 

A major pro is the open cooperative facet - this makes it incredibly easy to get to the table and get people playing as soon as it's set up, without extensive rule-explaining. All but the most casual gamers will enjoy; the premise and gameplay is straightforward and easy to understand. The length of turns is a slight drawback, particularly with inexperienced players, but most of our players have picked up quickly enough that the game starts to move along at a good pace. 

I would actually say the low difficulty is a drawback, and it's a good thing there are built in "more panic" options. It's nice to introduce a game that is nearly impossible to lose, but it becomes rather boring to keep playing a game with almost certain win conditions. Fortunately, it is pretty easy to adjust the difficulty level, but I would advise more serious gamers to jump right in to one of the higher-difficulty options, just to keep the pressure up.

RATING: 5
For a light game, Castle Panic is great if your having friends or younger family etc over and want to bring out a game that isnt too hard to explain or to play.
Castle Panic fills both of these requirements - rules can be explained in about 3-5 min (depending how fast you talk and the audience) and play is co-op and fast, so everyone can enjoy this game.
Of course, being a light "non-gamer" game, it doesnt have too much for the more serious gamer - for those types, i would recommend Battlestar or Pandemic, however if these serious gamers want to play with some non-gamers and not get the blank, dazed look during the rules explanation, then this game should be in their collection :-)

RATING: 8
I couldn't get rid of this game fast enough years ago.  But I looked into Cooperative Games again really in depth when our son was about 7 years old.  Some of the very things I didn't like about it from an adult perspective are what make it such a great game to play with kids.  Our son really enjoys it and its one of the games I have a lot of fun playing with our family.  I do enjoy it slightly better with 3 than with 2 since there are more options for trading a card (something either you can use this turn or see they can use on their next turn once monsters advance or even both ideally!).  We have never lost the game, even once, though we almost did on one occasion.  It's for that reason that I suggest picking up at least one expansion for the game (And I re-purchased this game knowing this requirement which I was less aware of when I initially got rid of my original copy).  That said we have played the base game a surprising number of times and still have fun with it.  Despite what some others have said I think the game doesn't feel too long.  Just about when it starts to its over in another couple turns or so.  Our 8 year old is actually ending up with all 3 expansions as Christmas presents from various people so we should have plenty of new Castle Panic challenges to conquer in the future.  I'm fairly confident I'll enjoy the expansions enough that I'd now play and suggest the games for an adult only group as well.  The base game though, by itself, I still wouldn't recommend without kids.

RATING: 6.5
Castle Panic is a cooperative, light strategy game for 1 to 6 players ages 10 and up.

Players must work together to defend their castle, in the center of the board, from monsters that attack out of the forest, at the edges of the board. Players trade cards, hit and slay monsters, and plan strategies together to keep their castle towers intact. The players either win or lose together, but only the player with the most victory points is declared the Master Slayer. Players must balance the survival of the group with their own desire to win.

RATING: 6
It's an interesting tower defense game where the player protect their castle from invading hordes of monster. The game is simple enough to be played with kids or non-gamers.

The game seems also very flexible because there are many variant rules and 1 expansion released so far. It's the kind of game that you want to have more stuff or more variety for replay value. Else, after a few plays, I imagine you could get bored.

My only complaint so far is that I think the boulder tiles are way too strong. I think the reason we won the game is because at least 2 boulders destroyed more than 3 monsters when passing. Monsters that would probably have done more damage than the boulders.

So I would probably buy the game if I could get it for sale or in a trade.

RATING: 6.5
Very simple in its concept, you are defending your castle against an invading army. Insted of playing one against the other, players have to team up against the game itself, sharing resources in order to beat it.
This variation allows for a completely competition-free game, where fun becomes more important than winning.
Rules are simple and well designed. Games tend to be smooth and are rarely one-sided.
Variants, provided along with core rules, allow different versions of the game, with different approaches, and different difficulty levels.
On the down side, there's really nothing more to it: one or two games and you'll have experienced everything this one has to offer.

In Castle Panic, if you play the variant that allows for an overall winner (if the players win, one of them is declared a champion), that keeps people from being able to push each other around--I want US to win, but I also want ME to win, so I'm going to make the decision that's best for me. RATING: 7.5
ÂüéÂ†°ÂÆàË°õÊà∞
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Castle Panic is a fun co-op game wherein players are working to defend a castle in the middle of the board from waves of attacking Trolls, Orcs, and Goblins.  Said castle is made up of pieces of cardboard on stands.  Each time the castle, or its outer walls, are hit you simply take one of the pieces away.  If you ever have to remove the last piece of castle you lose the game.

The invading armies attack in various sections around the board, as determined by a die roll.  These sections are colour coded.  There are also rings around the castle.  The invaders start at the outer ring and move ever closer to the middle ring where your castle sits.  To help players defend against the attackers, they play cards depicting one of either archers, swordsmen, or knights that can attack in their designated ring and colour.  There are other cards too that can reinforce or even rebuild sections of wall, or slow down or push back invaders.

Castle Panic is a fun, and easy to learn/play co-op game that can be played with young kids.  The tension builds quickly as more and more invaders appear on the board.  Right from the beginning you wonder how you will ward them all off and survive.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Good one to play with the kids...  plays like a virtual "king of the mountain" type game.   It has a fast pace and tension built into the mechanics.   It's a co-op game, but you can add a scoring system if you really need to have a winner.  The game plays fairly quickly and not complicated to learn or set up. 

It won't satisfy gamers that want a lot of "think" in their games.

Edit:  wasn't fast paced with 6 players and the expansions,  ugh!

RATING: 6
Game in a Nutshell: Co-op game of protecting your castle from mobs of baddies coming at you from all sides.

Played as: 4 player

Pros: Great theme that's well executed. The ability to play semi-cooperatively is a major part of the game that really brings the experience to another level. I like the presentation from artwork to graphic layout. No reason this shouldn't scale well from two to six players or even solo if that's your thing. Really, just an easy game to play with all types of people.

Cons: If played too cooperatively the game seems far too easy. So to that degree, the experience may vary greatly from group to group depending on how competitive they are among one another. On the other side, I imagine that played too un-cooperatively it could lead to an even more unsatisfying experience. As simple as the game is, there's just a few niggly rules requiring extra text on the board that seem to break the spirit of that nature.

Other: The game comes with a load of optional rules. I'd like to test more of those out going forward... especially all the ones that are supposed to add difficulty. Really, I think I've only left a couple of those difficulty rules out when playing, so likely next game will be all-in.

Best Use: Need more plays to say...

RATING: 10
I found Castle Panic while walking around the vendor area this year.  My wife pointed to it, and she said "I heard good things about that one." Later (not long before the vendor area closes), my wife was doing demos for other games,  I figured that I'd have some time to stop back and grab a copy of the game with good things.

The sales person was there along with Mr. Justin De Witt (the game designer, development, graphic art and design, etc).  I was asking Justin about the game, and he spoke very passionately about all the details (this is definitely his baby).  I bought the game, and asked him to sign my copy.  Justin was happy to do so, and I thought to myself that this is everything I love about (and why I support) the board game business.  It's accessible, friendly, and fun.  Good people, good games.  Justin invited us to play the game and have a chance to beat him (and have some snacks).  As much as my wife loves snacks, we were sadly not able to make it back for a castle attack.

After Origins (and a stormy drive home), I busted out my copy of the game at around 9:30 pm.  I figured I would assemble it all together, read the rules (or absorb it through osmosis), figure out single player setup, then head off to bed and ponder the game mechanics.  Hopefully, I would get a chance to play it the next day.  After opening and assembling it, easy breezy like, I picked up the rule book.  There's really not a whole lot of complicated things going on here.  I figure, hey, I'll do the setup so I can get that down then run through a quick turn.  I do so, and I think to myself, I can beat these guys. 

Suddenly, someone messed with the time-space continuum (probably that pesky Q - when will he ever respect humans and their needs).  It's now midnight, and my wife is home from the late shift wondering why I'm still up.  I can do this, that's why.  I can beat these damn Orcs and Trolls - first play through.  I had some good breaks, and I've lost three towers, but there's not many baddies left.  Someone has to stay up and finish the job.  Oh wait, job, and I have one tomorrow.  I finished the game, and I won, and it was intense.  It was every bit as intense as the instructions claim.  Man, I can beat them, I say, and I did, beat them, yeah, and I will beat them ... again ...

So, I crack it open after work the next day, and I throw it all up in seconds.  Soon, I'm pounding out Troll guts.  I get the baddie that summons three creatures - no problem.  Uhhh, I drew the summon 4 more token.  No problem, I beat this game yesterday.  Uhhh, I drew the summon 3 more token.  After finishing all the token draws along with the bad guy that moves everyone up a ring - I'm going down.  I know it, it's plain.  I'm going down, but I'm taking as many with me as I can.  It won't be a personal best by any means, but that Hero guy is looking at me.  I can't quit.  Sure, HE'S the Hero, but what will I be if I amscray?  I have to run it through to the bitter end.  Even after a killer draw with Barbarian, Redraw a card (Barbarian twice), Tar, Fortify, and a wall spackling job - I'm toast.  It was a proud yet futile stand.  The Trolls will talk about it as they digest my remains.  The count for me is one and one.

Yeah, I'm hooked.  It's an incredibly fun game.  Solo play is fantastic.  I downloaded the monster expansion.  I will buy any expansion for this game.  My head is coming up with new monster abilities automatically - how about a Grey Dragon that moves forward and rotates?  How about a Kobold that can move two spaces?  How about a Siren that will heal one point to one creature occupying the space after she moves?  It's addictive.  

Well done, Mr. De Witt, well done.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 2
Every once in a while, I feel compelled to rise and defend the honor of the co-op game from friends who dislike them.

They bring up the lack of tension.  "But wait!" I say.  "Clever games (like Betrayal at House on the Hill) weave elements of the unknown through the game, ratcheting up the tension!"

They bring up player quarterbacking.  "But wait!" I say.  "Clever games (like Elder Sign: Gates of Arkham) use a dynamic board and aggressive, quickly-shifting obstacles to ensure each player is the master of her or his own fate!"

They bring up uneven downtime.  "But wait!" I say.  "Clever games (like Space Alert) build in natural limits on downtime, and ensure that everyone gets in on the fun quickly!"

Then they bring up Castle Panic, and I have to go sulk in the other room.

RATING: 7
Castle Panic is an wonderful family game.  It's a cooperative game with a twist since there can be only one winner - the "Master Slayer."  Everyone needs to work together to stave off defeat but, at the same time, keep an eye out for opportunities to maximize your own VPs.  The rules are very well written and the important information is right on the board.  A big plus is that it plays in under an hour which is perfect for my family or as a "filler" between heavier and longer games.  I picked this game up on a whim and it exceeded my expectations.

RATING: 7
Huh. I generally don't like co ops because they're really hard and tend to beat down on the players, and some co ops just feel unbeatable due to luck (for example, drawing horrible events first+second turn in Robinson Crusoe), but this one was a lot easier to win, so I actually liked it more. A lot of people say co ops need to be hard to stay interesting, but I would prefer a smooth ride to the finish with my friends thats mildly hard, and this delivers.

Its still a bit simple so I worry a bit about replayability, and its not that many things you can do on your turn, but you can do enough that it kept me engaged and interested. Overall, I'm not crazy about co ops, but I would be willing to play this again if it hit the table, despite its lightness.

RATING: 2.5
Goblins and orcs and trolls - oh my!

Well...not so much 'oh my' as 'so what?', as it turns out. It's another co-operative game in a niche market that is in danger of becoming overloaded. The tacked-on competitive aspect is much derided, not least by me. And after being brought up on Hero Quest and its ilk then, frankly, three different types of monsters to fight isn't very many or exciting enough. I get the lasting impression that Castle Panic is really no more than a shell of a game - something that will be much better after proper customisation, but distinctly inadequate as it stands.

Kind of a let down, but easy enough to play with family. Interesting how it's both competitive and co-op, to a degree; if no one cooperates (and the towers fall), no one wins, otherwise the player with the highest score wins. Also interesting how you want to trade away good cards to help the team, but doing so can mean giving points to another player. It's OK as a family game, with kids.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Castle Panic is a cooperative game that, in terms of play, bears a certain resemblance to Forbidden Island.  Castle walls come down, but may be rebuilt, in the former just as portions of the island flood, but may be shored up again, in the latter, and players may trade cards among themselves to improve chances of group success in both games.  Castle Panic has a monsters-versus-the-knights-of-the-castle theme that appealed strongly to the 12 year old boys I played with.  The artwork on the board and cards is colorful and attractive, and all parts seem sturdy enough to stand up well to lots of play. The game created enough tension to maintain these kids' attention (no mean feat) and keep their adrenalin flowing.  They are a competitive lot, and not overly fond of cooperative games on principle, but they took to this one readily--especially with the body count at the end to determine who had been the most effective monster slayer.  I had a blast playing with them and especially enjoyed watching the level of cooperation gradually increase as the game progressed and they warmed to the idea of enlightened self-interest.  I had played a couple of solo games to learn the ropes ahead of time, and although I enjoyed them, I would have to say that this game is definitely more fun with several players.(3+4) Solo plays:2

RATING: 3
Almost completely random. This is something like 99% luck, 1% skill.

There's too much down time (with larger player counts), and nothing to do in your down time because you can't plan ahead. When it is your turn, there is usually a single, easily identifiable best move, so again there is no decision making involved. 

Some have suggested Castle Panic will be fun for children/non-gamers/stupid people, and thus fulfil a useful role by introducing folks to non-Monopoly etc. board games. However that doesn't make any sense to me - why not just play a good lighter game in the first place (like Ticket to Ride or Dominion)?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Draw a bunch of cards and hope that they match to the colour and area where the monsters are, which will allow you to whack them - so it's pretty luck based. You get to discard and redraw a card, and get to do a single card trade to alleviate some of the luck. Play your cards, then all the monsters move one area closer to the centre and you draw two more monsters. If they get to the centre without you collectively killing them, they whack the walls, and then the towers, until they run out of hit points and they die (hit points will be 1, 2 or 3 depending on the monster type) or run out of towers to wreck, at which point you lose. As you have 6 walls and 6 towers, it means a number of monsters need to make it to the middle without you getting them first, which is largely a product of of whether you get unlucky with all the monsters coming in one colour, or particularly bad draws in either the cards or the order in which monsters come out. So there doesn't seem like a lot of tension, but the game turns are fairly fast and is pleasant enough, if a bit long for what it is. It's ideal for my boys though, aged 8-11, who love the theme, love the whacking, don't mind the luck and love the idea that they're likely to win.

RATING: 7
"The base game is cute and fun, but is very simple and random, with not many decisions (at least as a pure co-op). The Wizard's Tower expansion adds a ton of interesting elements to the game, as well as lots of interesting decisions."

What I like:
- The cardboard castle is great for immersion
- Base game is very non-gamer friendly
- Often very tense, with winning or losing possible

What I don't like:
- Base game lacks interesting decisions
- Base game monsters are kind of dull

The expansion adds a lot of decisions, so for gamers it is a necessary expansion. I would put the base game weight around 1.6, and with the expansion I think it goes to 2.4.

RATING: 8.5
Rated after two plays (12/18/09) - Played last evening twice and had a blast.  I have heard someone describe Castle Panic as having a slight "videogame" feel to it and, after playing, understand what they are saying.  The action is pretty fast and furious as you try to keep the hordes at bay.  Game play is pretty simple and should work well with younger boys and girls (if they are cool with the fantasy theme).

I have heard some people say this game is easy - maybe it is, but it certainly wasn't last night.  2 games 2 losses and we weren't even close.  Whether that is an indication of bad luck or bad play (nah.... couldn't be that :D ) we shall see over more plays.

Update 1/2/10 : Have played several times lately with my sons and still having a lot of fun.  We have been playing "full co-op" and have managed to win (but just barely) the last several times.  I think my initial problem wasn't recognizing the values of keeping walls up.  Seems obvious now, but we were discarding too many lone Mortar/Brick cards instead of holding them until we had a match on the board.  Still an 8 for me in terms of fun.

RATING: 9.4
A huge luck component, but surprisingly fun for all that.  You'll often be sweating for a Barbarian or 'Barbarian Redux' (which for some curious reason is called Scavenge).

Yes, the strategy, such as it is, involves burning through your hand as much as possible every turn, and (for most of the game) trading to allow other players to do the same.  And yes, you can lose even though you all play a perfect co-op game.

But if you play a bad game then you'll almost certainly lose, so you do at least know that you've done it right.

And the co-op / competitive twist is just inspired.  You need to play co-operatively for most of the game to have any chance of winning, but at some point you have to make the decision to switch to selfish play, and the judgement of that is critical.

Do it too early and you'll all lose.  Do it overtly and the other players may freeze you out of trades.  Do it too well and one or more losing players might decide to throw the game and try to ensure that nobody wins.

I can't think of another game with such a subtle, neat mechanic that leads to such tense, emergent gameplay, and that excuses a lot.

However, I would strongly advise sticking with the basic game.  The Wizard's Tower expansion drowns the lilly in toxic gilding and detracts rather than adds to the basic larks.

RATING: 7.4
Solo Player Value = Excellent

Two Player Value = Excellent

Three Player Value = Excellent


Castle Panic is a very good cooperative game that offers challenging play and plenty of replay value.

Castle Panic is a good game.  Game play is hard describe though.  This is a light strategy game of central castle defense where monsters continually attack the castle from all sides.  Monsters are added with a chit-pull system.  Battle is handled through cards with a color coded and section system.  If the castle completely falls you lose.  The mechanics are simple yet elegant.  

But don't let the simplicity of the game fool you.  The game is rather difficult to beat.  The random nature of the game makes planning the defense of the castle impossible in the long term.  Players must handle each situation as it arises.  This is where players use the tool available to them to redraw cards and trade cards to mount the best defense each turn.  This forces the players to work together and really brings out the cooperative nature of the game.

I really enjoy the cooperative game play, but the game does have a slight element of competitiveness to it as well though.  While the players must work together for victory, the one player that fights and kills the most is the true winner.  For me this confuses the game.  I do not like when games are both cooperative and competitive.  A game should be one or the other, not both.  I take out the competitive part of the game and play fully cooperatively.  The players either win or lose as a team.  This makes the game much smoother.

The theme works well for the mechanics in the game.  It really elands itself to the environment.

The components are all nice.  The artworks cartoony, but well done.  Nothing extravagant here, just straight forward and workable.

The game is easy to learn and teach.  The rules are well written.  It is a great introductory game for new gamers, but still offers enough strategy to seasons gamers.



Pros - 
- Easy to teach and learn
- Simple mechanics that offer good strategy
- Difficult enough to keep you playing 


Cons - 
- Cooperative and competitive game play confuses the game.


Overall Playability = 7.2

Design = 8 
Strategy = 7
Luck = 6
Artwork & Components = 7
Use of Mechanics = 8
Time of Play = 7
Fun = 8
Innovation = 5
Analysis Paralysis = 8
Theme = 8


[b]------------------------------------------------------[/b]


[thing=104590][/thing] is the first expansion for Castle Panic.  

The Wizard's Tower adds to the game without detracting anything.  That is important for a good expansion.

And that is exactly what The Wizard's Tower is - a very good expansion.  

This expansion brings new, more powerful, monsters to the mix.  It also adds Mega Boss Monsters.  These are monsters that bend the rules a little and make the game more difficult.

The players get a second deck of cards to aid them in the fight.  These are Wizard Cards, or spells, that bring new powers to the players.  These cards are powerful and greatly help the players in the defense of the castle.

What makes this expansion so good is that the game remains perfectly balanced with the addition of the new monsters and Wizard Cards.  The power curve has not been thrown off in any way.  That is a true testament to the beauty of the design of this game.

I would say that not only it this expansion fantastic, it is the best way to play the game.

Adding The Wizard's Tower does change the score a bit

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.5
[color=#CC0000]  

My kids had almost zero interest when I got it at Christmas.  I'm planning to bring it out again after a cooling off period, but I think for the most part they didn't feel like they were an important part of the play.  There's two things that fundamentally rub against each other in its concept -- 

1.  All are one.  There's no guy on the board that represents [u]you[/u].  Branham's Razor ("this is me, these are mine") is violated and I think my two seven-year-olds didn't feel connected because of it.  My nine-year-old just seemed bored.

2.  The decisions are pretty simplistic.  There's generally an obvious greatest-need on the board and likely one best way to address it, so you trade your cards away to whomever needs them most and it's as likely as not that's not your decision to make.  This is true "multi-player solitaire" -- everyone agrees on how to solve the puzzle.

The advanced rules put a bit of interest into the game as they allow you to be greedy, but fundamentally they don't provide enough pressure on the concepts I just described above.  When we played my kids kept track of the kill-count, and that just made things worse because they were trading cards away to help someone else (a brother no less).  Not making the trade likely meant group failure.  That didn't appear much fun to them either.

I was very excited on the game when I heard about it and it got some great reviews from adults.  Alas, like more than a few kids games on the market, the ones that got good reviews from adults got very different reviews from my kids.  Likely I'll trade this one away.  A shame really, it seems like such a nice package.

S.

RATING: 6
This is like playing the Atari game [i]Space Invaders[/i], but instead of being attacked by alien spaceships, players are under siege in a castle fighting against hordes of monsters that keep coming and coming. It is nice as a cooperative game, but the mechanic of a winner between winners doesn't work at all here since creatures appear randomly, not necesary in the spots that you need, and there is not much control about what you can do in order to get points if you are not lucky, except exchange cards with other players. Then, well played, this will turn the game in a points transaction one. No one would ever give a card if he doesn't get a potential point in exchange, and no one will ever trade with whoever is in the lead. In fact, there is a chance that nobody ever exchange a card with anybody. And, since that could happen, then the game becomes a lottery, in which the surprise would be if the players are able to survive. So, [i]Castle Panic[/i] has to be played with the right attitude: Master Slasher, ok, but not to be taken seriously. Just relax, enjoy, have fun and slash some monsters, because life is just two days. And this is not because I'm not a "not so cooperative" kind of gamer. I like a lot [i]Cutthoat Caverns[/i] and [i][url=http://www.juegosdemesacr.com/cms/index.php?option=com_content&task=view&id=320&Itemid=1]Terra[/url][/i], and the idea of colaborate thinking in the moment to backstab your partners. I even like this mechanic in other games, like [i][url=http://www.juegosdemesacr.com/cms/index.php?option=com_content&task=view&id=58&Itemid=1]Arkham Horror[/url][/i] and [i]Defenders of the Realm[/i], but here it just doesn't fit.

RATING: 7
Every time I play Castle Panic I feel like it's a nail-biting experience. Walls fall within the first couple of rounds, we are constantly terrified of monsters getting past the walls and into the castle ring, and God forbid the dragon comes out (in the Wizard Tower expansion) and starts blasting fire everywhere.

Honestly, I really enjoy this game. It's easy to learn and simple to play. It's a great filler game when you're looking for something that won't take too much time or energy. And it's good fun when collaborating with your friends to figure out how on earth you're going to survive the next wave of monsters.

Though the board and box art are lacking, the rest of the art is solid and the orc and goblin fantasy theme works well as a setup to the gameplay. Ultimately the game is worth keeping in your collection as a solid, but light, collaborative experience for your game night.

I like watching them plot out the monster courses and make decisions about what trades will be best and help people on the current turn through 1 or 2 turns ahead. RATING: 6
An interesting take on the increasingly popular cooperative game, this time set in a castle surrounded by a forest full of monsters.  In one sense, this game has a feel similar to Ghost Stories, with a constant onrush of bad guys never giving you a break.  Unfortunately, all you do is play the cards you draw (and trade in a limited fashion) to defend the castle.  It lacks the movement with resulting choices of action from the previously mentioned game, which is something of step backward.  For the most part, you play every card you can every turn.  There are a few interesting tactical decisions to be made, which saves the game from absolute tedium.  I in general have a concern with any cooperative game that can be defeated by four newbies the first time through.  That does not bode well for future plays.

I think this would particularly work with younger players or those with less experience in the recent amazing crop of cooperative games.  This game really pales in comparison to that group.  Five years ago, things might have been different, though.  The other saving grace for the game is that there are multiple alternative rulesets included in the game, which may redeem the easy win we experienced.  So, the final verdict is that it is a pleasant enough distraction, but nothing I'm ever going to seek out. [01/13/2010]

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
1 play, 3er.

A very simple, somewhat bland semi-cooperative game (with variant rules to play full-coop, or 1-vs-many). Probably fun with non-gamers, but just wasn't terribly interesting.

--- Summary ---
The board is a set of 4 rings (forest, archer, knight, swordsman) with the castle in the center (6 towers protected by 6 walls), divided into 3 color zones (red, blue, green) and 6 wedges. Seed the board by placing 3 goblins (1HP), 2 orcs (2HP), and 1 troll (3HP) in the forest ring. On your turn, first draw cards up to hand limit (5). Then, optionally discard 1 and draw 1. Then, optionally trade 1 card with a player. Next, play cards from hand: most allow you to attack in a particular color/ring, doing 1 HP damage. Others modify attack, or allow you to rebuild destroyed wall, or other special effect. If you kill a monster, keep it as a trophy. Next, all remaining monsters advance one ring inward; if already at center circle, they move clockwise. If a monster hits a wall or tower, they destroy it and take 1HP damage. Finally, one at a time, draw 2 random monster tiles: if a monster, roll d6 and place in forest of appropriate wedge; if a special tile, resolve as needed (some move monsters inward, some around the board, etc.).

If all towers destroyed, players lose the game. If all 49 monsters are killed, the player with the best trophy collection (each is worth VP = HP of monster) wins.

RATING: 5
I'm hesitant to bad-mouth this game because it was a gift from a well-meaning friend who knew I wanted more cooperative games but it just simply isn't my cup of tea.

Castle panic is a VERY simple cooperative game where monsters move along concentric tracks outside your castle each turn in an attempt to breach your castle walls.  Each player takes a turn playing cards that attack these enemies, repair walls, or deploy their own sentries to stop the onslaught.  The goal is to survive the invasion.

There's just not much to this game to hold a group of adults attention unless they really are after a simpler game.  You can trade cards with your fellow players to deploy them at the most opportunistic moment but other than that there aren't many interesting choices to be made.  You choose what cards to play but most of the time those decisions are obvious.

The components, especially the 3D walls, are nice.  And as a family game to play with children this is a good gateway.  Not for a group of adults with discerning gaming tastes though.

RATING: 8
This is a fantastic game to play with kids. It's easy to teach, and the theme is a lot of fun. The decisions are mostly pretty simple--probably too trivial if playing with just adults--but there's just enough to think through that it doesn't feel as if the game is playing you.

We find the game pretty easy to beat with the basic rules, so we always draw 3 monsters per turn. Using this variant, our endings are almost always very close and tense, just as a co-op game should be. It also has the added bonus of making the game a little shorter, which is helpful when playing with kids.

RATING: 6
This is the type of game I would have LOVED when I was a young lad!  In fact, if my wee one was older than 3 weeks of age, I'd purchase this in a second. The production values of the game are top notch - the artwork is very fun and I particularly enjoy the castle walls.  It's a very well put-together game that is a great co-operative experience for kids, and adults might enjoy it too if they're looking for a bit of low mental energy fun.  I was trying to think if it might fit best within the "filler" category for adults, but I think there are games that suit that purpose much better.  Game design: 4/5  Personal enjoyment: 2/5  Total: 6/10

RATING: 7
Castle Panic is a very simple coop survival game.  I love the concept, and when I saw it on Will Wheaton's tabletop I knew I wanted a copy.  At the time I would have guessed this would rank a 9 or 10 on my list, but everytime I play it I generally like it less and less.  I think it gets a bit old because it is simple color matching and basic play order logic that plays out the same round after round.

Overall, it is a good simple coop game, but I feel like it has a bit less replayability than other coops out there.

Update: I see there are expansions for this, that might improve replay-ability, if so I will update and it might raise this to an 8

RATING: 5
A pretty game with an highly interesting "tower" defense theme. It appeals to most players and is easy to get to.

Despite its simple rules, it manages to create sufficient agony to the players and does have meaningful, if realatively easy, decisions to make. It generally keeps you well on your toes, as it should be.

The result is in the end a bit luck dependant due to the luck of the draw, but not so much that it is spoiling the game. Although the game appears to be best as a co-op, I think this is deceiving. There are tons of better coops out there, though few are a match in theme. I believe this game shines in overlord mode.

In the end what wins the day for me is the different playing modes. A two player overlord game (that I play against my wife) is an entirely different experience than a 5 player full co-op for example. And there is the default master slayer variant that seems a bit strange and I've yet to try it.

This game hits the table at a pace I never expected when I bought it.

RATING: 6
I went to BGG.CON with a list of over 100 games that I wanted to try, knowing that I'd never get to most of them. On the plane ride down to Dallas I was watching a new Board Games with Scott episode about Castle Panic, a game I'd never heard of previously, and that video alone convinced me to get out a pen and write Castle Panic into the extra small margins of my "games to try" list. Unlike most of the games on that list, I actually did get to try Castle Panic thankfully. I played with James, Lisa, and Brian, and I had a great time. I've been on the fence about whether to buy the game ever since. It's a cooperative game, and the fact that I already own and enjoy Ghost Stories, Pandemic, and Red November cuts both ways - on the one hand I might not need another cooperative game, but on the other hand I clearly like and enjoy cooperative games (and play them a lot given my 93 combined plays of the aforementioned three games). Castle Panic is simpler though, much simpler. It's actually so straightforward in terms of its gameplay that I think it only truly shines because of its competitive element. The players are theoretically working together to kill monsters that are slowly marching towards and destroying their walls and towers. However, like Krakow 1325 AD and Peter Hawes' upcoming War of the Roses, there is an undercurrent (or rip tide depending on who you're playing with) of selfish subterfuge. The player who individually kills the most monsters is named the "Master Slayer" (said best in a grandiose Scott Nicholson voice). I suppose it's up to the group how they want to interpret the "Master Slayer" appellation, but I personally think the game would thrive best by considering that person the sole winner. It injects into an otherwise overly simplistic game a wonderful element of tension and interaction. The players can't quite trust each other to always work for the good of the team rather than the good of themselves and thus won't take the optimal path to group victory by freely trading cards, but rather may horde them. You walk a dangerously fine line though because too much selfishness will cause everyone to lose and then nobody gets to be the "Master Slayer."
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5

RATING: 6
I played [thing=43443][/thing] together with the expansion [thing=104590][/thing], which I was told adds several elements to the base game, such as the named Wizard Tower, a deck of spells for the defenders, new creatures - some legendary - and some new effects; all of which make the game a whole lot better. The goal of the game remains the same: defend the fortress (walls and towers), while hordes of monsters come to attack it.

A player turn is pretty simple: first, draw cards until there are 5 in hand. Then is allowed to discard 1 card to draw another; and also trade cards with other players. Then, is possible to use as many cards as the player want - and most will attack the monsters, but several, specially when considering the spells deck, will have some neat effects. Normal attacks will cause 1 point of damage, and if the creature loses its last hit point, it leaves the board. Is important to know that the board is divided in sections (by colors - green, red and blue) and rings (by type of defender - archer, knight and swordsman - that can attack such place, plus the forest, where the creatures usually can't be hit) - so, for instance, a Red Archer will only be able to do damage to a creature in the red section in the archer ring. After the players uses his cards, the creatures on the board move (usually 1 space) in the direction of the fortress. If a one of them hits the walls, they take 1 damage and the wall is removed. If is a tower that is hit, the same happens, and once inside the walls, the creature start to move clockwise, destrying tower after tower, and only some special defenders cards can attack a creature inside the fortress, so be careful! Finally, 2 tokens are drawn from the bag (these can be new creatures or effects, like attacks from trebuchets and boulders, plagues, and so on) - if one or more of them are creatures, for each the player rolls a die, and puts the token in the corresponding place in the board, in the forest ring. Then, is the next player turn.

The game goes like this until the creatures destroy all the towers (keep the walls doesn't matter) or until the defenders kill all the of them (even after all the tokens in the bag were drawn, still is necessary to kill all that are on the board, threatening the fortress). In the first case, as expected, the players lose, in the second, players win. I know the game can be played competitively, but we didn't and, though I'm aware it enters in a semi-cooperative sort of game, in which everyone wins, but one is the win-est - this is not something I enjoy in games, with traitors I'm fine, but with "one win more" in coops, no, just no.

[thing=43443][/thing] counts, specially with the expansion, several effects coming from the enemies in order to breath some uneasiness, as the defenders can't really be sure, during the game (near the end, is possible), to know exactly what will be coming and when. Several creatures have special actions when they are drawn or in other moments (for instance, the Hydra, when hit, spawn new monsters; the Manticore, when it moves, it spits fire into the fortress; the Healer, when revealed, heals 1 point of damage of all the wounded creatures on the board; the Conjurer, when revealed, brings with him 1d6 Imps; and there are several others). The defenders, of course, also have special cards in their decks (both in the normal and in the Wizard deck), and with the spells they can cast fireballs, walls of force, hammers of light, chains of lighting, teleport, rains of ice, etc.

[thing=43443][/thing] showed itself as a better game than I expected it to be. What I read about it wasn't really all that good, but is likely that what brought the "surprise" for me was the expansion. Anyway, I was expecting a more childish tower defense cooperative game, with some pretty obvious decisions throughout, but, luckly, this wasn't the case (though, sometimes, the decisions is obvious, but not all the time).

[thing=43443][/thing] has its doses of luck, in the draw of the deck, in the draw of creatures and in the roll of the die to place them. But its main point is fixed: all the normal attacks, if able to hit, cause 1 point of damage - there is no chance of missing nor of not dealing damage. So, if a creature is on the board, it is possible to predict its advancement and strategize the best way to deal with it. And this is important to resist in some places and against some monsters. Also, the trading of cards is key in the game, and is the part that is really the cooperative in the game. This is true for simple situations like "Anyone has a Blue Knight, for me to kill that creature?" to some slightly more complex: "If I move this one together with that one, and toss some Tar in this one, I can trade this card with so in your turn you can use it when they are in the Swordsman ring to destroy both".

The components are good and functional, but nothing really pops (not a joke about the 3D towers and walls) too much, for good or bad. The art is well done and is made by the designer of the game, Justin De Witt, a talented guy.

So, overall, I enjoyed [thing=43443][/thing], as it has a nice level of challenge, and is possible, because of its easy rules, to be put quickly in the table and be played with groups ranging from kids to the veteran players (but, here, probably only really worth if adding the expansion). But I wasn't wowed by it, since I got to know much better cooperative games, with more meat and fun build into the gameplay - but most of these takes more time to be played. Anyway, I'm certainly willing to play [thing=43443][/thing] again, though I won't actively be looking for it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
I love the chaotic feel that's driven by the mechanic of flipping over two random monster tiles at the end of each turn, and by the dice rolls. You can have a great plan that gets ruined by having to rotate the monsters, or by having an unlucky dice roll that causes a boulder to go rolling through the only lane that you really didn't want it to roll through. A fun, lighter co-op game that plays well with 2 players.

RATING: N/A
Simple co-op (or semi co-op). Play your cards to deal damage to the bad guys in various quadrants and distances, the bad guys move forward and attack your castle if not eliminated. I liked the hand management and trading aspect, as you decided which cards to keep, which ones to trade to other players so that certain monsters could be eliminated when it got to their turn. It was fun as a problem solving co-op, the competitive aspects of the game held no interest for me. As the game wound down, I knew that technically I should stop trading with one player, and let the monster attack the castle, so that I'd win. But, I passed him the card, he killed the final monster, and "won" the game. I rejoiced in our shared victory.

17-8-2014 *update 3*
