15-8-2014 *update 2*
Played it with my girlfriend for the first time. I liked it better than the solo experience but I think with 3 or more its even nicer. With 2 players you can start planning the defense of the castle which you cant when you play solo. I rate this game 7 now for the 2 player experience.

31-7-2014 *UPDATE*
Had some spare time and decided to play a solo game. The first rounds went well. I even had times when there were none or only a few monsters on the board. I thought 'this is going to be easy'. I was wrong. I forgot about the bosses and the ''draw monster tokens''. At one point monsters were advancing from 5 out of 6 arcs and I drew most of the trolls at the last rounds. In the end I lost with 1 wall standing up and 5 monsters left on the board. Nice solo experience I have to say. Curious how it plays with a group. I Think the interaction will only bring this game to a higher level. For now I rate this game a 6.5. Will update again when I play this with 4 or up which will be next sunday.

30-7-2014
Got this in the mail today. After reading so much about it I decided to order it. Haven't played it yet but I will next sunday. Will update this comment after play. Components and artwork look very nice.

RATING: N/A
The forest is filled with all sorts of Monsters. They watched and waited as you built your Castle and trained your soldiers, but now they‚Äôve gathered their army and are marching out of the woods.
\13\\13\
Can you work with your friends to defend your Castle against the horde, or will the Monsters tear down your Walls and destroy the precious Castle Towers? You will all win or lose together, but in the end only one player will be declared the Master Slayer!
\13\\13\
Castle Panic is a cooperative, light strategy game for 1 to 6 players ages 10 and up.
\13\\13\
Players must work together to defend their castle, in the center of the board, from monsters that attack out of the forest, at the edges of the board. Players trade cards, hit and slay monsters, and plan strategies together to keep their castle towers intact. The players either win or lose together, but only the player with the most victory points is declared the Master Slayer. Players must balance the survival of the group with their own desire to win.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4
What you can do is completely dependent on which cards you draw, and the correct plays are glaringly obvious once you actually have the proper cards.

Strike One: Castle Panic isn't great - or anything close.

Strike Two:  The game is only half-cooperative, in that the evil forces can be vanquished through equal contribution of labor - yet the "winner" happens to be the person who landed the most finishing blows.  In a "we all deserve to die" suicide run like Terra, that's fine; but in a family game, it's just dumb.

(For those desiring an obscure reference, the Teenage Mutant Ninja Turtles game has the same underlying problem: competition where there should be cooperation.)

Strike Three:  Forbidden Island exists, and it's the better family game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
My initial assessment that this game would be fun for my family was correct.  The ability to trade cards both to the discard and with another player really adds to the co-op of the game.  My kids really got into the trading aspect by determining which cards would be best for what player at what time.  Of course, drawing monster movement tokens can disrupt those plans.  The random monster tile draws, random monster placement as well as the card draws will ensure an entirely different game each time it is played.  

I don't know if the game is brutal or if we just had bum luck, twice.  While the luck of the draw adds to the replayability, a bum draw could seriously hamper your efforts to defending the castle.  You need cards of both the right color (red, green, and blue) and distance (archer, knights, and swordsman) in order to damage the monsters.  And once they get into the keep, there are very few cards that can affect them.  A renegade monster in the tower without any cards to get him out spells disaster!
 
All-in-all, this is a great family co-op game.  I am sure with some of the more interesting variants it makes a great co-op game for adults as well.
